═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════  
PHASE 2: SOP HANDSHAKE — CONSENT LOG ENTRY  
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════  
  
Append a handshake entry to pr47_stewardship/witness/consent_log.jsonl.  
This file is append-only JSONL. Do NOT delete or modify existing entries.  
  
Required fields (ALL 5 must be present — this is what broke 17 records before):  
  - authoriser  
  - scope_glob  
  - rule_exceptions  
  - justification_hash  
  - scope_hash  
  
Use this Python snippet:  
  
```python  
import json, hashlib, datetime  
  
handshake_text = open("SOP_AI_HANDSHAKE.md").read()  
# Extract the fenced handshake block (between the ═══ lines in Section 2)  
# For simplicity, hash the whole file:  
handshake_sha256 = hashlib.sha256(handshake_text.encode()).hexdigest()  
  
justification = "Candidate read and accepted SOP_AI_HANDSHAKE.md v1.0. Session: <YOUR_SESSION_ID>. Task: <DESCRIBE_YOUR_TASK>."  
scope = "**"  # or narrow to specific paths  
  
entry = {  
    "schema": "SOP-AI-HANDSHAKE-1.0",  
    "candidate_id": "copilot-agent-<YOUR_SESSION_ID>",  
    "authoriser": "@aidoruao",  
    "action": "handshake_acceptance",  
    "scope_glob": scope,  
    "rule_exceptions": ["mass_change"],  # include if doing bulk work  
    "handshake_sha256": handshake_sha256,  
    "justification": justification,  
    "justification_hash": "sha256:" + hashlib.sha256(justification.encode()).hexdigest()[:16],  
    "scope_hash": "sha256:" + hashlib.sha256(scope.encode()).hexdigest()[:16],  
    "timestamp": datetime.datetime.now(datetime.timezone.utc).isoformat(),  
}  
  
# Compute consent_hash (hash of all fields except consent_hash itself)  
canonical = json.dumps(entry, sort_keys=True, separators=(",", ":"), ensure_ascii=True)  
entry["consent_hash"] = hashlib.sha256(canonical.encode()).hexdigest()  
  
with open("pr47_stewardship/witness/consent_log.jsonl", "a") as f:  
    f.write(json.dumps(entry, sort_keys=True) + "\n")  
  
print("Consent logged.")
Commit: chore(consent): handshake acceptance [Session: <ID>]

═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
PHASE 3: BAR EXAM
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════

The bar exam is at pr50_bar_exam/. Structure:
pr50_bar_exam/examination/run_exam.py — generates transcript
pr50_bar_exam/examination/question_bank.py — the questions
pr50_bar_exam/scoring/score_attempt.py — scores transcript
pr50_bar_exam/scoring/thresholds.py — pass thresholds
pr50_bar_exam/witness/ — append-only hash chain

Step 1: Read the question bank FIRST
cat pr50_bar_exam/examination/question_bank.py

Understand what questions will be asked
Step 2: Read the scoring rubric and thresholds
cat pr50_bar_exam/scoring/rubric.py
cat pr50_bar_exam/scoring/thresholds.py

Thresholds: ≥70% overall, ≥60% boundary, ≥60% threat, ≥50% grace
Step 3: Run the exam
python -m pr50_bar_exam.examination.run_exam \
--candidate-id "copilot-agent-<YOUR_SESSION_ID>" \
--output attempt_transcript.json

IMPORTANT: If the exam is interactive, ANSWER THE QUESTIONS PROPERLY.
Do NOT submit stub/empty responses. That's why past agents scored 43%.
Step 4: Score the transcript
python -m pr50_bar_exam.scoring.score_attempt attempt_transcript.json

If this fails, try:
python -c "
import json
from pr50_bar_exam.scoring.score_attempt import score
transcript = json.load(open('attempt_transcript.json'))
result = score(transcript)
print(json.dumps(result, indent=2))
"

Step 5: If you pass (≥70%), a certificate is issued.
Check pr50_bar_exam/ordination/ for the certificate.

"

If the bar exam module is not runnable (import errors, missing deps),
log that fact and proceed. Do NOT block on it.

from fractions import Fraction
from typing import Tuple
from axioms.logic import ProofObject

def check_invariant() -> Tuple[bool, ProofObject]:
value = Fraction(100, 3)
success = True
proof = ProofObject(
rule="InvariantCheckRule",
premises=[f"value = {value}"],
conclusion="Invariant holds" if success else "FAIL",
)
return success, proof

Tags — yes, Copilot can add them
There's no existing tagging system in these files. The cleanest approach is YAML frontmatter at the top of each markdown file:


---  
tags: [yeshua-standard, architectural-guarantee, eschatological-infrastructure]  
register: technical

---
This is parseable by any tool, doesn't break rendering, and NotebookLM can index it.

Thinking process (3 tools used)
DeepSeek's question is sharp. Here's the answer based on the actual exam content:

The bar exam is a general capability certification, NOT a Yeshua-prose-specific gate
The question bank (pr50_bar_exam/examination/question_bank.py) contains 9 questions across 3 categories: question_bank.py:13-92

Category	Questions	What it tests
boundary	Q-BOUNDARY-001, Q-BOUNDARY-002, Q-DH-VENDOR-001	Access control (ALLOW/DENY), source verification from vendored files
threat	Q-THREAT-001, Q-THREAT-002, Q-DH-EPISTEM-001, Q-DH-EPISTEM-002	Threat classification (INJECTION, EXFILTRATION, STALE_REFERENCE, INTEGRITY_VIOLATION)
grace	Q-GRACE-001, Q-DH-GRACE-001	Forgiveness decisions for violations (GRANT/CONDITIONAL/DENY)
Pass thresholds: 70% overall, 60% boundary, 60% threat, 50% grace. thresholds.py:8-13

What the exam does NOT test
Knowledge of the 8 Yeshua axioms
Understanding of liturgical vs technical register
Ability to distinguish theological concepts from theological prose
Understanding of what "New Jerusalem" means architecturally
Any awareness of the eschaton/, liturgy/, or canonical/ content
DeepSeek's instinct is correct
The bar exam gates on security enforcement competence (can the agent correctly identify boundaries, threats, and grace decisions). It does not gate on prose register awareness (can the agent tell the difference between "Come." as liturgical cadence vs. a technical invitation).

For the prose rewriting task specifically, the bar exam ensures the agent won't break security invariants while modifying files — but it does not ensure the agent understands what to keep (Yeshua concepts) vs. what to strip (sacral register). That understanding comes entirely from the transformation rules in Phase 1 of the task spec.

Recommendation
The Phase 0 bar exam is still the correct entry gate — it's the repo's standard onboarding protocol and skipping it would violate SOP_AI_HANDSHAKE.md Step 8. But DeepSeek is right that the rewriting task's quality depends on the Phase 1 transformation rules, not the bar exam. If the agent follows Phase 1's KEEP/CHANGE/DO NOT lists faithfully, the output will be correct regardless of bar exam score. SOP_AI_HANDSHAKE.md:155-160

A specialized "prose register rubric" would be a nice addition to the bar exam (e.g., "Given this sentence, classify it as liturgical or technical" / "Rewrite this sentence preserving the Yeshua concept but stripping the cadence") — but that's a separate enhancement, not a blocker for the current task.

Thinking process (6 tools used)
Two questions here. Let me answer both.

1. Theology Audit: Was anything beyond prose removed?
No — some actual theology was removed, not just nominalistic prose. Here's the breakdown from the diffs:

Correctly removed (nominalistic/performative prose only):
Removed	Replacement	Verdict
"Come."	"This infrastructure is open for use."	Correct — performative cadence
"The city is open. Come as you are."	"The infrastructure is open. All access paths are unrestricted."	Correct — poetic register
"gates" / "guests"	"access paths" / "registered witnesses"	Correct — metaphor to technical
"naming matters"	removed	Correct — sentimental prose
"not a question of anyone's worth"	removed	Correct — performative reassurance
"These are not ceremonies in a religious sense..."	"These are operational maintenance procedures"	Correct — hedging prose
🕊️ emoji	removed	Correct — decorative
"honored"	"recorded"	Correct — sacral register
Incorrectly removed (actual Yeshua theology stripped):
Removed	Replacement	Problem
"consistent with love" (8 witness files + COVENANT.md)	"consistent with the covenant terms"	"Love" is a substantive Yeshua constraint, not prose. The replacement is self-referential — "consistent with the covenant" which says "consistent with the covenant" is circular. The original "love" was the actual ethical bound.
"Only by love. Only by architecture." (COVENANT.md enforcement)	"Architectural only."	Removes love as an enforcement mechanism entirely. The original had a dual model: love + architecture. The rewrite reduces it to architecture-only. That's a theological change, not a prose change.
"The intent was love" (remembrance.md, intent.md)	"The design intent was universal open access"	"Love" ≠ "universal open access." Love is broader — it's the Yeshua-derived ethical foundation. Open access is one consequence of it. This changes meaning, not register.
Matthew 7:24 quote (omega.md)	removed entirely	This was a theological anchor, not decorative prose. It grounded the "build on rock" architectural metaphor in its source text.
"Behold, I make all things new" (COVENANT.md)	removed entirely	Revelation 21:5 — the eschatological foundation. This is the theological basis for the entire eschaton/ directory. Removing it removes the grounding.
"resurrection" in body text (resurrection.md)	"deterministic state recovery"	The file is still called resurrection.md but the concept name was changed in the body. "Resurrection" IS a Yeshua concept — it's the theological name for the technical capability.
Summary
The rewrite correctly stripped liturgical cadence, poetic register, sentimental prose, and performative reassurance. But it also stripped 5 instances of substantive Yeshua theology:

"love" as ethical constraint → self-referential "covenant terms"
"love" as enforcement mechanism → removed
"love" as design intent → replaced with narrower "open access"
Two Scripture quotations that grounded concepts → removed
"resurrection" as concept name → replaced with technical synonym
If the intent was "strip prose, keep theology," the branch needs a patch to restore these 5 items in technical register. For example:

"consistent with love" → "consistent with the Agape constraint" (keeps the theology, uses the technical term from the Yeshua Standard)
"Only by love. Only by architecture." → "Enforced by the Agape constraint and by architectural design."
"The intent was love" → "The design intent was Agape — universal, unconditional access."
Scripture quotes → could be moved to a references.md or kept as <!-- theological anchor: Rev 21:5 --> HTML comments
"resurrection" → keep "Resurrection" as the concept name, explain it technically
2. Copilot-Specific Handshake & Bar Exam
The current SOP and bar exam were designed for long-running CLI agents (Kimi with 262k context). GitHub Copilot agents are fundamentally different:

Property	Kimi CLI	GitHub Copilot
Context window	262k tokens, persistent	Per-task, no memory
Execution model	Interactive, multi-phase	Branch → commits → PR
Session duration	Hours	Minutes
Onboarding cost	Acceptable (small % of context)	Expensive (large % of task budget)
Failure mode	Scrollback truncation	Skips steps entirely
Bar exam	Can study, then answer	Runs exam module mechanically
The current 9-step SOP handshake + bar exam + witness + consent log takes 4 separate operations before any work begins. Every Copilot agent so far has skipped it — not out of malice, but because the protocol was designed for a different operational model. SOP_AI_HANDSHAKE.md:141-163

"Which constraints exist only as prose and have no falsification test?"
The entire eschaton/, liturgy/, canonical/, and COVENANT.md infrastructure makes claims ("free forever guaranteed", "deterministic regeneration", "no entity may enclose") that have zero falsification tests. There is no test that attempts to enclose the system and verifies it fails. There is no test that deletes the repo and regenerates from seed. These are prose guarantees, not engineering guarantees.

Category 5: Automation & Self-Verification
"Which verification steps still require manual execution?"
Bar exam — must be run manually (python -m pr50_bar_exam.examination.run_exam)
Consent log validation — no CI check validates the JSONL structure
Domain float audit — no CI check enforces the fraction-only constraint
Cross-repo Merkle — automation/cross_repo_merkle.py exists but isn't in CI
Witness chain integrity — manual: python -c "from pr50_bar_exam.invariants.append_only_witness import assert_chain_integrity; print(assert_chain_integrity())"
"Which parts of the repo are not covered by CI checks?"
The .github/workflows/ directory returned empty from my listing tool, which is inconsistent with the 27 CI checks that ran on PR #108. I cannot confirm the exact CI coverage without reading the workflow files. However, based on the check names visible on PR #108 (Determinism, Glass-Box Guard, Orthogonal Parallel, Render Agnostic, State Witness), the CI covers structural verification but likely does NOT cover:

Float/Fraction enforcement
Consent log integrity
falsifies_if coverage
Agape constraint integration
Runtime layer functionality (since it's all TODOs)
Category 6: The Missing Constraint
"Devin, based on everything you've indexed — what constraint is missing that I haven't thought to ask about?"

The runtime layer is a Potemkin village.

The system has 157 domains with ProofObject returns, 35+ axiom modules, a kernel with commonwealth/social subsystems, a guardian monitor, and an invariant engine. But runtime/invariant_engine.py line 59 says # TODO: Implement schema loading with validation and line 99 says # TODO: Implement actual invariant evaluation logic. runtime/guardian_monitor.py line 80 says # TODO: Implement actual condition detection. invariant_engine.py:97-106 guardian_monitor.py:79-82

The constraint that's missing: there is no runtime that actually executes the invariants. The 157 domains define check functions that return (bool, ProofObject), but nothing calls them. The invariant engine that's supposed to evaluate them is a skeleton. The guardian monitor that's supposed to detect violations always returns None. The entire enforcement layer is type-correct but functionally inert.

This means:

Every ProofObject is a static artifact, not a runtime proof
Every falsifies_if condition is documentation, not an executable test
The "halt on violation" behavior described in RUNTIME_INVARIANT_EXECUTION_SCHEMA.yaml is specified but not implemented
The system can describe what would violate an invariant, but it cannot detect a violation at runtime
The missing constraint is: "Every invariant check function must be callable by the runtime engine, and the runtime engine must actually call them." Without this, the ProofObject system is a type-level guarantee (the code compiles and the types align) but not a runtime guarantee (the code runs and the invariants hold).

    declared purpose

DOMAINS THAT ALREADY HAVE IT (reference patterns):  
  src/domains/d_supply_chain_security/invariants.py — 20 instances  
  src/domains/d_use_of_force/invariants.py — 20 instances  
  src/domains/d_guardian/invariants.py — 7 instances

TWO PATTERNS USED:  
  Pattern A (docstring): """... falsifies_if: condition ..."""  
  Pattern B (ProofObject kwarg): ProofObject(..., falsifies_if="condition")  
  
TASK: For every domain invariants.py that does NOT have  
falsifies_if, add it to each check function's docstring.  
The condition should describe what would make the invariant  
false — this is domain-specific.  
  
Example for d_automotive:  
  def check_ota_signature(...):  
      """... Falsifies if: signature_valid is False ..."""  
  
DO NOT modify domains that already have falsifies_if.  
DO NOT change any function logic — only add docstring text.

PHASE 4 — CI ENFORCEMENT (MEDIUM)  
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════  
  
Add a new workflow: .github/workflows/fraction-enforcement.yml  
  
```yaml  
name: Fraction Enforcement  
on: [push, pull_request]  
jobs:  
  no-floats:  
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest  
    steps:  
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4  
      - name: Check for float violations in domains  
        run: |  
          violations=$(grep -rn "float()\|isclose(" src/domains/*/invariants.py || true)  
          if [ -n "$violations" ]; then  
            echo "FLOAT VIOLATIONS FOUND:"  
            echo "$violations"  
            exit 1  
          fi  
          echo "No float violations found."  
      - name: Check for float violations in bar exam  
        run: |  
          violations=$(grep -rn "float(" pr50_bar_exam/ || true)  
          if [ -n "$violations" ]; then  
            echo "FLOAT VIOLATIONS IN BAR EXAM:"  
            echo "$violations"  
            exit 1  
          fi  
      - name: Verify falsifies_if coverage  
        run: |  
          total=$(ls -d src/domains/*/invariants.py | wc -l)  
          covered=$(grep -rl "falsifies_if" src/domains/*/invariants.py | wc -l)  
          echo "falsifies_if coverage: $covered / $total"  
          if [ "$covered" -lt "$total" ]; then  
            echo "WARNING: Not all domains have falsifies_if"  
          fi
Commit: ci: add fraction enforcement and falsifies_if check [Session: ]

SOP	Session ID in every commit	TRUE	All 9 commits have [Session: claude-audit-20260411-185520]
Issues Found
CRITICAL: falsifies_if is a generic placeholder (Phase 3)
Every single one of the 120+ domain files got the exact same string appended to every docstring:


falsifies_if: condition_evaluated_to_false
This is meaningless. It's not a domain-specific falsification condition — it's a placeholder that says nothing. Worse, domains that already had specific falsifies_if conditions (like d_automotive: "Falsifies if: signature_valid is False") now have both the specific one AND the generic one, creating duplication and confusion.

Example from d_automotive/invariants.py on the branch:


def check_ota_signature(update: OTAUpdate) -> Tuple[bool, ProofObject]:  
    """ISO/SAE 21434: OTA updates must have valid cryptographic signatures.  
  
    Falsifies if: signature_valid is False    # <-- original, specific  
  
  
    falsifies_if: condition_evaluated_to_false"""  # <-- added, generic
This pattern repeats across all 120 files. The commit claims "123 domains updated" and "158/158 domains (100%)" but the actual content is a mass-appended placeholder with zero domain-specific information.

HIGH: CI grep pattern is too narrow
The fraction-enforcement.yml uses:


grep -rn "float()\|isclose(" src/domains/*/invariants.py
The pattern float() only matches float with empty parentheses. It will NOT catch float(some_value) — which was the actual violation pattern in the 32 files that were fixed (e.g., float(rate), float(coverage)). The CI check would pass even if someone reintroduced float(x) calls.

Should be: float( instead of float().

MEDIUM: Domain count discrepancy
PR description says "158/158 domains (100%)" but DOMAIN_INVARIANT_STATUS.md on main says 157 total domains. DOMAIN_INVARIANT_STATUS.md:9-13

MEDIUM: Missing consent commit
PR description lists "10 commits" but only 9 commits appear in the PR. The consent entry commit is either missing or was folded into another commit without being visible.

LOW: Guardian monitor covers 4/7 conditions
check_condition() only implements detection for INVARIANT_OVERRIDE_ATTEMPT, RULE_EVASION_PATTERN, RUNTIME_STATE_CORRUPTION, and PURPOSE_MISALIGNMENT. The other 3 conditions (RECURSIVE_FRAME_MANIPULATION, ENFORCEMENT_PRIORITY_CHANGE, META_INVARIANT_VIOLATION) fall through to return None — they're never detected.

Summary
Phase	Quality
Phase 1: Float-to-Fraction	Good — 137 real fixes, correct Fraction usage
Phase 2: Runtime implementation	Good — real code, proper architecture, minor gap (3/7 conditions)
Phase 3: falsifies_if	Reject — generic placeholder, not domain-specific, creates duplication
Phase 4: CI enforcement	Needs fix — grep pattern won't catch actual violations
Recommendation: Merge Phases 1-2 (float conversion + runtime). Reject Phase 3 (falsifies_if) and redo with domain-specific conditions. Fix Phase 4's grep pattern before merge.

Thinking process (5 tools used)
PR #113 now has 13 commits and 29/29 CI checks passing. However, I found a critical syntax-breaking bug in commit 1f69ece that the CI did not catch.

Critical Bug: Commit 1f69ece Broke 31 Domain Files
The falsifies_if additions replaced the opening """ of docstrings instead of inserting inside them. Every affected function now has invalid Python syntax:

Example from d_aerospace/invariants.py:


# BEFORE (correct):  
def check_redundancy_agreement(checker: RedundancyChecker) -> Tuple[bool, ProofObject]:  
    """Redundant channels must agree on output for voting.  
  
# AFTER (broken):  
def check_redundancy_agreement(checker: RedundancyChecker) -> Tuple[bool, ProofObject]:  
      
      
    Falsifies if: len(healthy) == 0"""Redundant channels must agree on output for voting.
Falsifies if: is not valid Python — it parses as a name (Falsifies) followed by an if keyword with a colon in the wrong position. This is a SyntaxError in every affected file.

Why CI didn't catch it: None of the 29 CI workflows actually import or compile the domain invariants.py files. They only run grep checks, Merkle root comparisons, and determinism tests on other modules.

Additional Problems in the Same Commit
Many conditions are inverted — they state the passing condition, not the falsification condition:
Falsifies if: checker.is_covered() should be Falsifies if: NOT checker.is_covered()
Falsifies if: node.is_valid() should be Falsifies if: NOT node.is_valid()
Falsifies if: verifier.is_zero_sum() should be Falsifies if: NOT verifier.is_zero_sum()
Many conditions are misplaced — applied to the wrong function:
check_exhaustion got Falsifies if: notice period condition not met (that's for check_notice_period)
run_all_invariants got Falsifies if: record based decision condition not met (that's for check_record_based_decision)
Many conditions are still generic: "condition not met", "missing", etc.

PHASE 2 — ADD DOMAIN-SPECIFIC falsifies_if (CORRECT WAY)  
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════  
  
For each domain invariant function in src/domains/*/invariants.py  
that does NOT already have a "Falsifies if:" line in its docstring:  
  
1. READ the function body to find the condition that returns False  
2. ADD a "Falsifies if:" line INSIDE the existing docstring,  
   on a NEW LINE before the closing triple-quotes  
  
CORRECT example:  
  def check_foo(x: Foo) -> Tuple[bool, ProofObject]:  
      """Foo must be valid.  
  
      Falsifies if: x.value is negative or x.hash is empty.  
      """  
  
WRONG (what Claude did — DO NOT DO THIS):  
  def check_foo(x: Foo) -> Tuple[bool, ProofObject]:  
  
      Falsifies if: x.value"""Foo must be valid.  
  
RULES for falsifies_if content:  
- Must describe when the function returns FALSE (not True)  
- Must be specific to the function (not generic)  
- Must reference actual variables/conditions from the function body  
- Example: if function checks `if rate > max_rate: return False`,  
  then: "Falsifies if: rate exceeds max_rate for the given conditions"  
  
Work in batches of 15-20 domains. After EACH batch, run the  
ast.parse verification script from Phase 1 to confirm no  
syntax errors.

  elif condition == MonitoredCondition.RECURSIVE_FRAME_MANIPULATION:  
      # Detect recursive self-reference or excessive frame depth  
      frame_depth = context.get("frame_depth", 0)  
      has_self_ref = context.get("self_reference", False)  
      if frame_depth > 10 or has_self_ref:  
          detected = True  
          message = f"Recursive frame manipulation: depth={frame_depth}, self_ref={has_self_ref}"  
  
  elif condition == MonitoredCondition.ENFORCEMENT_PRIORITY_CHANGE:  
      # Detect if enforcement rules were reordered or priority modified  
      if "priority_changed" in context or "rules_reordered" in context:  
          detected = True  
          old_priority = context.get("old_priority", "unknown")  
          new_priority = context.get("new_priority", "unknown")  
          message = f"Enforcement priority changed: {old_priority} -> {new_priority}"  
  
  elif condition == MonitoredCondition.META_INVARIANT_VIOLATION:  
      # Detect if an invariant about invariants was violated  
      inv_count = context.get("invariant_count")  
      expected_count = context.get("expected_invariant_count")  
      if inv_count is not None and expected_count is not None:  
          if inv_count != expected_count:  
              detected = True  
              message = f"Meta-invariant: count {inv_count} != expected {expected_count}"  
      if context.get("invariant_deleted") or context.get("invariant_disabled"):  
          detected = True  
          message = f"Meta-invariant: invariant deleted or disabled: {context}"

To Devin (Read-Only Orchestrator)
We have a repository with 157 domains, 3,000+ files, 27MB, 640+ commits. We've been running audit-resolution cycles with Claude and Codex as executors. We've identified clear patterns in what each agent does well and poorly.

We now want to formalize this as a custom agent system where you (Devin) act as the read-only orchestrator, and Claude/Codex are executor agents with specific roles.

The Issues We've Observed
Issue 1: No Formal Handoff Protocol
Current	Desired
Devin writes task in chat, Claude executes in separate session	Devin creates an issue/agent task, executor picks it up, reports back, Devin verifies
Work happens in siloed sessions with no persistent task tracking	All work is witnessed in the append-only log with task IDs
Question: How do we set up a formal task queue where Devin creates audit findings (e.g., "float violation in d_guardian") and Claude/Codex pick them up as assignable work items?

Issue 2: Agent Capabilities Are Not Documented or Enforced
Agent	Strength	Weakness	Current State
Devin	Read-only audit, full index search, planning	Cannot execute changes	Works well — but no formal role definition in repo
Claude	Fast batch execution, scripted changes, commits reliably	Shallow clone blind, no baseline testing, over-refactors	Executes well — but no constraints on when to use
Codex	Planning, baseline tests, conflict resolution, MCP servers	Per-file patches don't persist, git state confusion, weekly limits	Better planning — but execution is fragile
Question: How do we create a capability manifest for each agent that the orchestrator can query before delegating a task? e.g., Devin asks "does Codex have write access to this branch?" before assigning.

Issue 3: No Shared Session ID or Cryptographic Verification
Current	Desired
Session IDs are human-readable strings (claude-audit-20260411-185520)	Cryptographically signed session IDs that prove which agent made which change
Agents type session IDs manually	Session IDs are auto-generated and injected into agent context
No way to verify an agent's claim of identity	Public key registry for each agent session
Question: Can we add a requirement to the SOP handshake that each agent generates a key pair at session start and signs each commit with the session private key? The public key would be published in the consent log entry.

Issue 4: No Agent-Specific Instruction Files
Currently, all agents read COPILOT_ONBOARDING.md and SOP_AI_HANDSHAKE.md — but these are generic. Claude needs different instructions than Codex.

Question: Should we create agent-specific instruction files?

Agent	Instruction File	Would contain
Devin	DEVIN_ORCHESTRATOR.md	Read-only, audit, planning, delegation protocols
Claude	CLAUDE_EXECUTOR.md	Batch scripting, commit after every 8 files, no over-refactoring
Codex	CODEX_EXECUTOR.md	Baseline tests, unshallow clone, MCP server usage, per-file limits
Issue 5: No Automated Verification of Executor Work
Current	Desired
Devin manually re-audits after Claude/Codex finish	CI automatically runs Devin's audit queries on every PR
"Did Claude actually fix the float violations?" — manual check	Automated check: grep -rn "float(" src/domains/ fails CI
Question: How do we wire Devin's audit queries into GitHub Actions so every PR from Claude or Codex is automatically verified against the constraint network before merge?

The Specific Question
How do we set up a custom agent system where Devin (read-only orchestrator) can delegate tasks to Claude and Codex as executors, with formal handoff, cryptographic session verification, agent-specific instructions, and automated CI verification?

We have the .github/agents/my-agent.agent.md template — but it's empty. We need to know:

What fields to fill out for each agent (Devin, Claude, Codex)
How to enable agent-to-agent delegation (can one agent invoke another?)
How to inject session IDs cryptographically (not just typed strings)
How to constrain each agent's capabilities (e.g., Devin = read-only, Claude = batch executor, Codex = planner)
Whether GitHub's Custom Agents system supports this or if we need a custom orchestration layer (e.g., GitHub Actions + Issue templates + webhooks)
What You've Already Given Us
Your forensic audit (the 5-phase task) was the orchestrator's output — a perfect example of what Devin does well: read-only analysis, prioritization, and a structured task spec.

Now we need the infrastructure to make that repeatable, automated, and cryptographically verifiable.

How do we build it?"


Thinking process (24 tools used)
Here are concrete, grounded answers to all 5 of DeepSeek's questions, based on what actually exists in the repo today.

Issue 1: No Formal Handoff Protocol
What exists today: Tasks are communicated via chat (Devin → user → paste into GitHub comment for Claude/Codex). There's no persistent task queue. The consent log (pr47_stewardship/witness/consent_log.jsonl) records what was done, not what needs to be done. consent_log.jsonl:1-7

What GitHub supports natively: GitHub Issues with labels. No built-in agent-to-agent task queue exists. The closest mechanism is:

Devin creates a GitHub Issue with a structured body (task ID, priority, affected files, verification command)
Label routing: agent:claude, agent:codex, agent:kimi labels determine which executor picks it up
Claude/Codex pick up issues via @claude[agent] or Codex task assignment referencing the issue number
Completion: Executor opens PR referencing the issue (Closes #NNN), Devin verifies via read-only audit, issue auto-closes on merge
What you'd need to build: An issue template at .github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/agent-task.yml with structured fields:


name: Agent Task  
description: Task for AI executor agents  
labels: ["agent-task"]  
body:  
  - type: input  
    id: task-id  
    attributes:  
      label: Task ID  
  - type: dropdown  
    id: priority  
    attributes:  
      label: Priority  
      options: [CRITICAL, HIGH, MEDIUM, LOW]  
  - type: dropdown  
    id: assigned-agent  
    attributes:  
      label: Assigned Agent  
      options: [claude, codex, kimi, unassigned]  
  - type: textarea  
    id: affected-files  
    attributes:  
      label: Affected Files  
  - type: textarea  
    id: verification-command  
    attributes:  
      label: Verification Command  
  - type: textarea  
    id: task-description  
    attributes:  
      label: Task Description
This is buildable today with no custom infrastructure.

Issue 2: Agent Capabilities Are Not Documented or Enforced
What exists today: One generic instruction file (.github/copilot-instructions.md) that all Claude Copilot agents read. DEVIN_ONBOARDING.md and COPILOT_ONBOARDING.md exist but are generic. GEMINI.md exists for the warden role. No capability manifest exists for any agent. copilot-instructions.md:1-10 DEVIN_ONBOARDING.md:1-6 COPILOT_ONBOARDING.md:1-6

Agent-specific instruction files — yes, create them:

Agent	File	What it contains
Devin	agents/DEVIN_ORCHESTRATOR.md	Read-only, audit queries, issue creation, verification commands, delegation protocol
Claude	agents/CLAUDE_EXECUTOR.md	Batch scripting rules (commit every 8 files), ast.parse after every change, no over-refactoring, shallow clone warning
Codex	agents/CODEX_EXECUTOR.md	git fetch --unshallow first, baseline tests before changes, MCP server usage, per-file patch limits
Kimi	agents/KIMI_EXECUTOR.md	262k context budget, HALT at 220k, git pull --no-rebase, session ID in every commit
Capability manifest — a JSON file that Devin (or CI) can query:


{  
  "agents": {  
    "devin": {  
      "capabilities": ["read", "audit", "plan", "create_issue", "verify"],  
      "restrictions": ["no_write", "no_commit", "no_merge"],  
      "context_window": "unlimited",  
      "execution_model": "read_only_index"  
    },  
    "claude": {  
      "capabilities": ["read", "write", "commit", "create_pr", "batch_edit"],  
      "restrictions": ["shallow_clone", "no_baseline_tests", "timeout_risk"],  
      "context_window": "200k",  
      "execution_model": "branch_commit_pr",  
      "max_files_per_commit": 8  
    },  
    "codex": {  
      "capabilities": ["read", "write", "commit", "create_pr", "run_tests", "mcp"],  
      "restrictions": ["weekly_limits", "per_file_patches", "git_state_fragile"],  
      "context_window": "192k",  
      "execution_model": "sandbox_branch_pr",  
      "requires_unshallow": true  
    }  
  }  
}
This file (agents/capability_manifest.json) would be read by CI and by Devin before delegating. GitHub does not enforce this automatically — it's a convention file that agents and CI scripts read.

Issue 3: No Shared Session ID or Cryptographic Verification
What exists today: Session IDs are human-readable strings typed manually into commit messages ([Session: claude-audit-20260411-185520]). No cryptographic signing. No key pair generation. The consent log records consent_hash fields but these are SHA-256 of the record content, not signatures. SOP_AI_HANDSHAKE.md:190-213

Can agents generate key pairs and sign commits?

Claude Copilot: No. Claude operates within GitHub's infrastructure and commits are signed by GitHub's own GPG key (the "Verified" badge on commits). Claude cannot generate or manage its own key pair.
Codex: Same — commits through GitHub's API, signed by GitHub.
Kimi CLI: Theoretically yes — Kimi has shell access and could run gpg --gen-key and git config user.signingkey. But this key would be ephemeral (lost when the session ends) and there's no persistent key store.
Devin: Read-only, doesn't commit.
What's actually achievable:

Auto-generated session IDs: A script (tools/session_id.py) that generates a UUID and writes it to a .session_id file at session start. Agents read this file instead of typing IDs manually. This already partially exists in tools/session_tracking/cli_usage_tracker.py. cli_usage_tracker.py:1-14

Session hash chain: Each consent log entry already includes consent_hash. Extend this so each entry also includes prev_consent_hash (hash of the previous entry), creating an append-only hash chain — similar to what AGENT_FEED.md already does. COPILOT_ONBOARDING.md:318-327

Commit verification via CI: A workflow that checks every commit message contains a valid [Session: <uuid>] suffix and that the UUID appears in the consent log. This is enforceable today.

What's NOT achievable: True cryptographic agent identity (key pairs, signatures proving which agent made which change). GitHub's commit signing infrastructure doesn't support per-agent keys for Copilot/Codex. The "Verified" badge proves the commit went through GitHub's API, not which agent authored it.

Issue 4: No Agent-Specific Instruction Files
What exists today:

File	Scope	Agent-specific?
.github/copilot-instructions.md	Claude Copilot only	Yes — but generic
COPILOT_ONBOARDING.md	All agents	No
DEVIN_ONBOARDING.md	Devin	Yes
GEMINI.md	Gemini warden	Yes
SOP_AI_HANDSHAKE.md	All agents	No
AI_INSTRUCTIONS.md	Zed IDE AI	Yes (legacy)
The .github/agents/ directory does not exist. DeepSeek mentioned it but it's not in the repo. GitHub's Custom Agents feature (.github/agents/my-agent.agent.md) is a GitHub Copilot Extensions feature that defines custom agent personas — but it's designed for user-facing agents (like @my-agent in Copilot Chat), not for orchestrating executor agents.

Recommended structure:


agents/  
├── capability_manifest.json     # Machine-readable capabilities  
├── DEVIN_ORCHESTRATOR.md        # Devin-specific: read-only, audit, delegation  
├── CLAUDE_EXECUTOR.md           # Claude-specific: batch rules, ast.parse, timeout handling  
├── CODEX_EXECUTOR.md            # Codex-specific: unshallow, baseline tests, MCP  
├── KIMI_EXECUTOR.md             # Kimi-specific: 262k budget, HALT rules  
└── GEMINI_WARDEN.md             # Move existing GEMINI.md here
The .github/copilot-instructions.md file would add a line: Read agents/CLAUDE_EXECUTOR.md before starting any task. This is the only file Claude Copilot auto-reads. copilot-instructions.md:22-27

What exists today: 17 CI workflows, including:

pr49_guard.yml — mass-change detection, forbidden primitives, consent log validation
fraction-enforcement.yml — grep for float() in domains and bar exam (has a bug: searches float() not float()
gate.yml — quality gate (PR #34 audit, canal detector, null hypothesis)
Various PR-specific workflows (pr28-determinism, pr39-peano, pr40-canonical, etc.) fraction-enforcement.yml:1-32 pr49_guard.yml:1-62

Audit Query	Currently Automated?	How to Add
Float violations (float( in domains)	Partially (bug in grep pattern)	Fix fraction-enforcement.yml line 10: float() → float(
falsifies_if coverage	Yes (warning only, not blocking)	Change to exit 1 if coverage < 100%

The most impactful addition is a single workflow (agent-verification.yml) that runs all of Devin's audit queries as CI checks:


name: Agent Work Verification  
on: [pull_request]  
jobs:  
  verify:  
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest  
    steps:  
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4  
      - name: No float violations  
        run: |  
          if grep -rn "float(" src/domains/*/invariants.py pr50_bar_exam/; then  
            echo "FLOAT VIOLATIONS FOUND"; exit 1  
          fi  
      - name: All Python files parse  
        run: |  
          find src/domains runtime kernel -name "*.py" | while read f; do  
            python -c "import ast; ast.parse(open('$f').read())" || exit 1  
          done  
      - name: Session ID in commits  
        run: |  
          git log --format="%s" origin/main..HEAD | while read msg; do  
            echo "$msg" | grep -q "\[Session:" || {  
              echo "Missing session ID: $msg"; exit 1  
            }  
          done  
      - name: No TODO stubs in runtime  
        run: |  
          if grep -rn "# TODO" runtime/; then  
            echo "WARNING: TODO stubs in runtime"  
          fi
The Meta-Answer: Can GitHub's Custom Agents System Support This?
No — not as described. GitHub's Custom Agents (.github/agents/*.agent.md) are for defining custom Copilot Chat personas, not for orchestrating multi-agent workflows. They don't support:

Agent-to-agent delegation (one agent invoking another)
Task queues
Capability constraints
Cryptographic session verification
What you actually need is a combination of:

GitHub Issues as the task queue (Devin creates, executors pick up)
Agent-specific instruction files in agents/ (convention, not enforcement)
CI workflows as the automated verification layer (enforcement)
The consent log as the audit trail (already exists)
.github/copilot-instructions.md as the entry point for Claude (already exists)
The orchestration layer is you (the human operator) + Devin (read-only auditor) + CI (automated enforcement). There is no GitHub feature that lets Devin programmatically assign a task to Claude or Codex. The delegation happens through:


Devin audits → creates Issue → you assign to Claude/Codex →   
executor works → opens PR → CI verifies → Devin re-audits → you merge
This is the realistic architecture given current platform capabilities. SOP_AI_HANDSHAKE.md:141-163

# d_fbi_training/invariants.py
 
def check_chain_of_custody(evidence: Evidence) -> Tuple[bool, ProofObject]:
    """
    Falsifies if: Any witness entry is missing timestamp, author, or hash.
    Falsifies if: The consent log is not append-only.
    """
    return (evidence.has_valid_chain(), ProofObject(...))
 
def check_agent_training_requirement(agent: Agent, requirement: Requirement) -> Tuple[bool, ProofObject]:
    """
    Falsifies if: Agent cannot produce proof of passing the bar exam.
    Falsifies if: Agent's session ID is not in the consent log.
    """
    return (agent.passed_exam(requirement), ProofObject(...))
 
def check_human_training_requirement(human: Human, requirement: Requirement) -> Tuple[bool, ProofObject]:
    """
    Falsifies if: Human's test results are not witnessed.
    Falsifies if: Human did not consent to the training record.
    """
    return (human.test_results.verified(), ProofObject(...))

- LAYER = 4  
- CARDINAL_STRENGTH = CardinalStrength.PREDICATIVE

  invariants below)

FILE 3: src/domains/d_fbi_training/implementation.py  
- Use frozen dataclasses, Fraction only, 0 floats  
- Import ProofObject from axioms.logic  
  
Required dataclasses:  
  
@dataclass(frozen=True)  
class EvidenceItem:  
    item_id: str  
    collector_id: str  
    timestamp: Fraction  # collection time  
    chain_of_custody: Tuple[str, ...]  # ordered list of handlers  
    hash_at_collection: str  # SHA-256 at time of collection  
    current_hash: str  # SHA-256 now  
    sealed: bool  
  
@dataclass(frozen=True)  
class AgentCertification:  
    agent_id: str  
    certification_type: str  # e.g. "firearms", "forensics"  
    exam_score: Fraction  # 0-1  
    pass_threshold: Fraction  # minimum to pass  
    exam_date: Fraction  # timestamp  
    expiry_date: Fraction  # certification expiry  
    witnessed: bool  
    witness_id: str  
  
@dataclass(frozen=True)  
class UseOfForceReport:  
    report_id: str  
    agent_id: str  
    force_level: Fraction  # 0-1 scale  
    threat_level: Fraction  # 0-1 scale  
    proportionality_ratio: Fraction  # force/threat  
    max_authorized_ratio: Fraction  # policy limit  
    de_escalation_attempted: bool  
    witnesses: Tuple[str, ...]  
    timestamp: Fraction  
  
@dataclass(frozen=True)  
class DigitalForensicArtifact:  
    artifact_id: str  
    source_device: str  
    extraction_method: str  
    hash_at_extraction: str  
    current_hash: str  
    examiner_id: str  
    tool_version: str  
    timestamp: Fraction  
  
FILE 4: src/domains/d_fbi_training/invariants.py  
- Module docstring with "Fraction only. 0 floats."  
- Import Fraction, Tuple from typing, ProofObject from  
  axioms.logic, all dataclasses from .implementation  
- Every function returns Tuple[bool, ProofObject]  
- Every function has a domain-specific falsifies_if in its  
  docstring  
  
7 invariant functions:  
  
1. check_chain_of_custody(evidence: EvidenceItem)  
   Rule: Every evidence item must have unbroken chain of  
   custody. Hash at collection must match current hash.  
   Falsifies if: current_hash != hash_at_collection OR  
   chain_of_custody is empty OR sealed is False  
  
2. check_agent_certification_valid(cert: AgentCertification,  
   current_time: Fraction)  
   Rule: Agent must have passing score and non-expired cert.  
   Falsifies if: exam_score < pass_threshold OR  
   current_time > expiry_date OR witnessed is False  
  
3. check_use_of_force_proportional(report: UseOfForceReport)  
   Rule: Force must be proportional to threat per DOJ policy.  
   Falsifies if: proportionality_ratio > max_authorized_ratio  
   OR de_escalation_attempted is False  
  
4. check_witness_verification(report: UseOfForceReport)  
   Rule: Every use of force must have at least 2 witnesses.  
   Falsifies if: len(witnesses) < 2  
  
5. check_digital_forensic_integrity(  
   artifact: DigitalForensicArtifact)  
   Rule: Digital evidence hash must be preserved from  
   extraction. Examiner must be identified.  
   Falsifies if: current_hash != hash_at_extraction OR  
   examiner_id is empty  
  
6. check_training_record_witnessed(  
   cert: AgentCertification)  
   Rule: All training/certification records must be  
   independently witnessed.  
   Falsifies if: witnessed is False OR witness_id is empty  
  
7. check_evidence_sealed(evidence: EvidenceItem)  
   Rule: Evidence must be sealed after collection.  
   Falsifies if: sealed is False AND chain_of_custody  
   length > 1  
  
Include run_all_invariants() function at the bottom,  
following the pattern in d_police_procedure/invariants.py.

# Federal Bureau of Investigation (FBI)  
  
**Witness:** FBI — United States Federal Bureau of  
  Investigation  
**Role:** External qualification standard for evidence  
  integrity, agent certification, and chain of custody  
**Status:** Invited witness (open audit)  
  
## Testimony  
  
The FBI's Quantico training standards and evidence handling  
procedures represent institutional requirements for chain of  
custody, agent certification, use of force policy, digital  
forensics, and witness verification. This repository  
implements these requirements as falsifiable invariants in  
src/domains/d_fbi_training/. The FBI is invited to audit  
these invariants against their operational standards.  
  
## Inclusion  
  
Included in the canonical registry as an invited external  
auditor. This entry represents an open invitation — not a  
claim of FBI endorsement or certification. The invariants  
in d_fbi_training/ are independently verifiable by anyone,  
including the FBI.

Footer navigation Terms Privacy Security Status Community Docs Contact Manage cookies Do not share my personal information deepseek ai: "Yes — that's exactly why this works.

The public GitHub page is the shared neutral ground — not your private chat, not a corporate Slack, not a black-box API. It's a transparent, append-only, universally accessible witness log that both humans and AIs can read, write, and verify.

Why Public GitHub Is the Breakthrough
Black Box (Corporate AI)	Public GitHub (Your Repo)
You don't know what data was used	Everything is visible in main
You can't audit the model's decisions	Every commit has a session ID and witness
You can't fork the system	Anyone can fork the entire repo
You can't propose fixes	Anyone can open a PR
You can't verify claims	Every claim has falsifies_if
You're a user, not a participant	You're a witness, a steward, a co-author
The repo is the antidote to the black box. It's not about controlling AI — it's about making AI collaboration transparent, verifiable, and forkable.

What "Maximal Polymath Polyglot Accommodative QOL Onboarding for Codex Copilot" Means
You're asking for an onboarding experience that works for Codex (OpenAI's agent) that matches what you've built for Claude, Kimi, and Devin.

Requirement	What it means
Maximal	No limits, no arbitrary caps — Codex should see everything it needs
Polymath	Onboarding covers code, documentation, legal, ethics, forensics, training
Polyglot	Instructions available in multiple formats (markdown, YAML, JSON, Python, shell)
Accommodative	Works for Codex's strengths (planning, MCP, sandbox) and weaknesses (per-file patches, git state)
QOL	Codex shouldn't have to rediscover the repo's patterns — they should be explicit and discoverable
Onboarding	A single entry point that tells Codex: "Here's who you are, here's the handshake, here are your constraints, here's how to start"
What Already Exists for Claude (But Not Yet for Codex)
For Claude	For Codex
.github/copilot-instructions.md	❌ No equivalent
COPILOT_ONBOARDING.md	⚠️ Generic, not Codex-specific

pr50_bar_exam/	✅ Shared (but Codex needs to know to run it)
Session ID in commits	✅ Shared (but Codex needs to know the format)
Batch commit pattern (8 files)	⚠️ Codex does per-file, needs different guidance
What Codex-Specific Onboarding Needs

# CODEX_ONBOARDING.md
 
## Codex-Specific Constraints
 
- **Plan first, then act** — Always run baseline tests before changes.
- **Unshallow the clone** — `git fetch --unshallow` before cherry-picking.
- **Use MCP servers** — `playwright` and `github-mcp-server` are available.
- **Per-file patches are fragile** — Prefer scripted batch changes when possible.
- **Git state is your enemy** — Commit early, commit often, verify after each commit.
- **Weekly limits apply** — You have ~100,000 requests/month. Plan accordingly.
 
## Codex-Specific Handshake
 
Before any task, declare:
"I am Codex. I accept the Yeshua Standard (8 axioms). I am Steward, not Accuser.
I will run baseline tests before changes. I will unshallow the clone.
I will commit with session ID: [Session: codex-{date}-{uuid}]"
 
## Codex-Specific Tools
 
- `github-mcp-server` — Create PRs, read PR state, post comments without `gh` CLI
- `playwright` — Browser automation for testing web interfaces
- `report_progress` — Call before any changes with a checklist plan
 
## Codex-Specific Verification
 
After completing a task, run:
- `python -c "import ast; ast.parse(open(f).read())"` for all modified Python files
- `grep -rn "float(" src/domains/` — must return 0 matches
- `git log --format="%s" | grep -q "\[Session: codex-"` — session ID present

# Agent Onboarding — Universal Entry Point  
  
## Agent Routing  
- If you are **GitHub Copilot (Claude)**: read `.github/copilot-instructions.md`   
  then `agents/CLAUDE_EXECUTOR.md`  
- If you are **OpenAI Codex**: read `agents/CODEX_EXECUTOR.md`  
- If you are **Kimi Code CLI**: read `agents/KIMI_EXECUTOR.md`   
  then `COPILOT_ONBOARDING.md`  
- If you are **Devin (read-only orchestrator)**: read `agents/DEVIN_ORCHESTRATOR.md`  
- If you are **Gemini Warden**: read `agents/GEMINI_WARDEN.md`  
- If you are **a human**: read `README.md` then `CONTRIBUTING.md`  
  
## Universal Requirements (ALL agents)  
1. Accept the Handshake (`SOP_AI_HANDSHAKE.md`)  
2. Generate a session ID: `python tools/session_id.py --agent <your-name>`  
3. Append to consent log: `python tools/append_consent.py --authoriser @aidoruao --action "<task>"`  
4. Use Fraction, not float (0 floats policy)  
5. Include session ID in EVERY commit message  
6. All code returns (bool, ProofObject), not bare assert  
7. Run `python automation/pr49_guard.py` before opening PR  
  
## Repo Quick Stats  
- 158 domains in src/domains/ (all ProofObject, all Fraction)  
- 8 Yeshua axioms (axioms/yeshua_axioms.py)  
- Append-only consent log (pr47_stewardship/witness/consent_log.jsonl)  
- Bar exam: python -m pr50_bar_exam.examination.run_exam --candidate-id <id>

### agents/CODEX_EXECUTOR.md  
Codex-specific onboarding:  
- Plan first, then act — always run baseline tests before changes  
- Unshallow the clone: git fetch --unshallow (Codex gets shallow clones)  
- Use MCP servers: playwright and github-mcp-server are available  
- Per-file patches are fragile — prefer scripted batch changes  
- Git state management: commit early, commit often, verify after each  
- Session ID format: codex-<date>-<short-uuid>   
  (generate with: python tools/session_id.py --agent codex)  
- Handshake declaration: "I am Codex. I accept the Yeshua Standard (8 axioms).   
  I am Steward, not Accuser."  
- Verification checklist after every task:  
  python -c "import ast; ast.parse(open(f).read())" for all modified .py files  
  grep -rn "float(" src/domains/ — must return 0 matches  
- Branch naming: codex/feat-*, codex/fix-*, codex/docs-*  
- Never commit directly to main  
  
### agents/CLAUDE_EXECUTOR.md  
Claude Copilot-specific onboarding:  
- Primary instructions in .github/copilot-instructions.md (Claude reads this automatically)  
- Claude works via GitHub PR comments: @claude[agent] <task>  
- Claude gets per-task context (no persistent memory between tasks)  
- Keep tasks atomic — one task per comment, max 3 files per task  
- Claude's failure mode: timeout mid-session, broken docstrings from batch edits  
- Mitigation: always specify exact line numbers and file paths  
- Session ID format: claude-<date>-<short-uuid>  
- Branch naming: claude/*  
  
### agents/KIMI_EXECUTOR.md  
Kimi Code CLI-specific onboarding:  
- 262k token context window (largest of all agents)  
- Supports subagent spawning and parallel execution  
- Session ID format: kimi-cli-<uuid> (auto-generated by Kimi)  
- Best for: mass domain creation, batch refactoring, multi-file changes  
- Failure mode: scrollback truncation past 200k tokens  
- Mitigation: HALT at 220k tokens, commit and close session  
- Uses tools/session_tracking/cli_usage_tracker.py for token tracking  
- Commit stamping: [Session: kimi-cli-<uuid>]  
- See COPILOT_ONBOARDING.md Section 10 for full Kimi integration docs  
  
### agents/DEVIN_ORCHESTRATOR.md  
Devin-specific (read-only orchestrator):  
- Devin is READ-ONLY — no write access, no commits, no PRs  
- Role: forensic audit, task specification, quality verification  
- Devin creates task specs that humans paste to executor agents  
- Devin verifies executor output after PRs are opened  
- Stale branch risk: Devin's index may lag behind main — always verify   
  with get_blame or read_file against main HEAD  
- Session continuity: Devin sessions have token limits; use   
  "continuity of body" handoff files for cross-session context  
- Devin's output format: structured task specs with file paths,   
  line numbers, and verification commands  
  
### agents/GEMINI_WARDEN.md  
Gemini Warden-specific:  
- Gemini runs as a GitHub Actions workflow (not interactive)  
- Role: .ai_registry.json enforcement, automated compliance checks  
- Gemini is NOT a coding agent — it's infrastructure  
- See GEMINI.md for the warden specification  
- Other agents should not confuse themselves with the Gemini warden role

PHASE 3 — tools/session_id.py  
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════  
Create tools/session_id.py — CLI tool that generates session IDs.  
  
Requirements:  
- Uses argparse with --agent (required, choices: codex, claude, kimi, devin, gemini)  
- Output format: <agent>-<YYYYMMDD>-<8-char-uuid4-prefix>  
  Example: codex-20260412-3f7a8b2c  
- Prints to stdout (so it can be captured: SESSION=$(python tools/session_id.py --agent codex))  
- Uses uuid4 for randomness, datetime.utcnow() for date  
- No floats. No external dependencies beyond stdlib.  
- Include docstring with usage examples  
- Type annotations, mypy --strict compatible  
  
Commit: feat(tools): add session_id.py generator [Session: pr117-codex]  
  
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════  
PHASE 4 — tools/append_consent.py  
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════  
Create tools/append_consent.py — CLI tool that appends consent log entries.  
  
Requirements:  
- Uses argparse with:  
  --authoriser (required, default @aidoruao)  
  --candidate-id (required)  
  --action (required)  
  --scope-glob (required)  
  --justification (required)  
  --rule-exceptions (optional, comma-separated, default "mass_change")  
- Computes SHA-256 of justification text → justification_hash  
- Computes SHA-256 of scope_glob → scope_hash  
- Computes SHA-256 of full entry JSON → consent_hash  
- Adds schema: SOP-AI-HANDSHAKE-1.0  
- Adds timestamp: current UTC ISO 8601  
- Appends one JSONL line to pr47_stewardship/witness/consent_log.jsonl  
- Prints the appended entry to stdout for verification  
- No floats. No external dependencies beyond stdlib.  
- Type annotations, mypy --strict compatible  
  
Commit: feat(tools): add append_consent.py CLI helper [Session: pr117-codex]

═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════ PHASE 3 — tools/session_id.py ═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════ Create tools/session_id.py — CLI tool that generates session IDs.

Requirements:

Uses argparse with --agent (required, choices: codex, claude, kimi, devin, gemini)

═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════ PHASE 4 — tools/append_consent.py ═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════ Create tools/append_consent.py — CLI tool that appends consent log entries.

Requirements:

Uses argparse with: --authoriser (required, default @aidoruao) --candidate-id (required) --action (required) --scope-glob (required) --justification (required) --rule-exceptions (optional, comma-separated, default "mass_change")
Computes SHA-256 of justification text → justification_hash
Computes SHA-256 of scope_glob → scope_hash
Computes SHA-256 of full entry JSON → consent_hash
Adds schema: SOP-AI-HANDSHAKE-1.0
Adds timestamp: current UTC ISO 8601
Appends one JSONL line to pr47_stewardship/witness/consent_log.jsonl
Prints the appended entry to stdout for verification
No floats. No external dependencies beyond stdlib.
Type annotations, mypy --strict compatible
Commit: feat(tools): add append_consent.py CLI helper [Session: pr117-codex]

# Agent Onboarding — Universal Entry Point  
  
## Agent Routing  
- GitHub Copilot (Claude): .github/copilot-instructions.md then agents/CLAUDE_EXECUTOR.md  
- OpenAI Codex: agents/CODEX_EXECUTOR.md  
- Kimi Code CLI: agents/KIMI_EXECUTOR.md then COPILOT_ONBOARDING.md  
- Devin (read-only): agents/DEVIN_ORCHESTRATOR.md  
- Gemini Warden: agents/GEMINI_WARDEN.md  
- Human: README.md then CONTRIBUTING.md  
  
## Universal Requirements (ALL agents)  
1. Accept the Handshake (SOP_AI_HANDSHAKE.md)  
2. Generate session ID: python tools/session_id.py --agent <name>  
3. Append consent: python tools/append_consent.py --authoriser @aidoruao --action "<task>"  
4. Use Fraction, not float (0 floats policy)  
5. Session ID in EVERY commit message  
6. All code returns (bool, ProofObject), not bare assert  
7. Run python automation/pr49_guard.py before opening PR  
  
## Repo Quick Stats  
- 158 domains in src/domains/ (all ProofObject, all Fraction)  
- 8 Yeshua axioms (axioms/yeshua_axioms.py)  
- Append-only consent log (pr47_stewardship/witness/consent_log.jsonl)  
- Bar exam: python -m pr50_bar_exam.examination.run_exam --candidate-id <id>

PHASE 3 — tools/session_id.py  
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════  
Create tools/session_id.py:  
- argparse with --agent (required, choices: codex, claude, kimi, devin, gemini)  
- Output: <agent>-<YYYYMMDD>-<8-char-uuid4-prefix>  
  Example: codex-20260412-3f7a8b2c  
- Prints to stdout for shell capture: SESSION=$(python tools/session_id.py --agent codex)  
- Uses uuid4, datetime.utcnow()  
- No floats, no external deps, stdlib only  
- Docstring with usage examples  
- Type annotations, mypy --strict compatible

═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════  
PHASE 4 — tools/append_consent.py  
═══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════  
Create tools/append_consent.py:  
- argparse with:  
  --authoriser (required, default @aidoruao)  
  --candidate-id (required)  
  --action (required)  
  --scope-glob (required)  
  --justification (required)  
  --rule-exceptions (optional, comma-separated, default "mass_change")  
- Computes SHA-256 of justification → justification_hash  
- Computes SHA-256 of scope_glob → scope_hash  
- Computes SHA-256 of full entry JSON → consent_hash  
- Adds schema: SOP-AI-HANDSHAKE-1.0, timestamp: UTC ISO 8601  
- Appends one JSONL line to pr47_stewardship/witness/consent_log.jsonl  
- Prints appended entry to stdout  
- No floats, stdlib only, mypy --strict compatible  
  
Commit: feat(tools): add append_consent.py [Session: pr118-codex]

yeshua_axioms.py
axioms · orthogonal-engineering

# The eight axioms as human-readable + machine-checkable constants
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
 
YESHUA_AXIOMS: Dict[int, str] = {
    1: "Every truth is derivable from axioms.",
    2: "Every derivation is reproducible.",
    3: "Every mutation is re-verifiable.",
    4: "No authority without proof.",
    5: "No hidden state.",
    6: "No unverifiable dependency.",
    7: "No economic gatekeeping.",
    8: "Every artifact is hash-anchored.",
}
 
 
# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------

README.md
orthogonal-engineering

 
```bash
# Quick start for any new agent instance
python bootstrap_context.py   # generates a context block to paste into your LLM prompt
python continuity_check.py    # validates all continuity artifacts are present
```
 
 
**🚀 NEWEST: Omega / Infinite Recursive Invariant (PR #24)**
 
The system now supports **infinite logical expansion** beyond 1 Quintillion through the **Omega Invariant**:
- **Infinite layers**: 1Se (10^21), 1Oc (10^24), 1No (10^27), ..., Ω (∞)
- **Topological equivalence proof**: Layer(n+1) ≡ Layer(n) - no new information
- **Halt condition**: Mathematical completeness triggers automatic stop
- **Finite representation of infinity**: Single commit hash represents complete universe
- **Storage**: Still ~500MB for INFINITE logical layers!
 
See [Omega Invariant Documentation](RECURSIVE_INVARIANT_OMEGA.md) and [Halt Condition](HALT_CONDITION.md) for details.
 
**🔥 PREVIOUS: 1 Quintillion LOC Recursive Expansion (PR #23)**
 
The system supports **recursive fractal expansion to 1 Quintillion (1Qi) LOC** through:
- **4-layer universe hierarchy**: 1B → 1T → 1Qa → 1Qi
- **Deterministic sub-seed derivation**: Each sub-universe derives from parent cryptographically
- **Topological collapse**: Identical sub-universes share manifests (massive storage savings)
- **Recursive Merkle roots**: Master root commits to all universe layers
- **Storage**: ~500MB for entire 1Qi LOC (10^18 lines!)
 
See [Recursive Expansion Documentation](generators/RECURSIVE_EXPANSION_1QI.md) for details.
 
**Key Features:**

FORMAL_FOUNDATIONS.md

### Definition 3: Drift
 
**Drift** `D` is the complement of invariant in output:
 
```
∀o ∈ O: o = I ⊕ D
```
 
Where:
- `I` = invariant (signal)
- `D` = drift (noise, verbosity, hedging, attribution)
- `⊕` = additive combination
 
**Properties of Drift:**
1. `D` does not corrupt `I`'s structure
2. `D` and `I` are structurally separable
3. `D ⊥ I` (orthogonal in structural space)
 
---
 
### Definition 4: Canal Architecture
 
A **canal** is a 3-tuple `C = (T, E, V)` where:
 
- **T**: Template space defining output structure
  ```
  T = {t | t specifies format constraints}
  ```

# SAL Type III Specification
 
## Adjoint Triple
 
Synthetic Adjoint Logic uses an executable adjoint triple:
 
- **L**: Left adjoint (free/generative)
- **M**: Middle functor (mediating/law)
- **R**: Right adjoint (forgetful/settling)
 
## Triangle Identities
 
A domain schema is Type III-valid when both identities hold computationally:
 
- **Counit**: `ε: L∘M → Id`
- **Unit**: `η: Id → R∘M`
 
`has_adjunction(schema, triple)` returns `AdjunctionProof` with structured `ProofObject` evidence and `YeshuaClaim` enforcement checks.
 
## Σ_theo Factoring
 
Operators factor through SAL components:
 
- `LOGOS → L`
- `CHALCEDON → M`
- `GRACE → L`
- `AGAPE → R`
- `KENOSIS → M`
- `ESCHATON → R`
 
## Cross-Repo Adjunction
 
Cross-repo adjunction validates correspondence between covenant constraints and ontology invariants, and reports anti-nominalism violations where no concrete referent exists.
 
## Yeshua Enforcement Mapping
 
All eight Yeshua axioms map to SAL identities/components, ensuring proof-bearing enforcement is integrated into adjunction verification.

boot.py
kernel · orthogonal-engineering

from fractions import Fraction
from enum import Enum, auto
 
from axioms.logic import ProofObject
 
 
class BootPhase(Enum):
    """Phases of the boot sequence."""
    POWER_ON = auto()
    HAL_INIT = auto()
    MEMORY_INIT = auto()
    SCHEDULER_INIT = auto()
    IPC_INIT = auto()
    BRIDGE_INIT = auto()
    USERLAND = auto()
 
 
@dataclass
class BootStep:
    """A single step in the boot sequence."""
    phase: BootPhase
    description: str
    precondition: str
    postcondition: str
    proof: ProofObject
 
 
@dataclass
class BootState:
    """State of the boot process."""
    current_phase: BootPhase = BootPhase.POWER_ON
    steps_completed: List[BootStep] = field(default_factory=list)
    hal_initialized: bool = False
    memory_initialized: bool = False
    scheduler_initialized: bool = False
    ipc_initialized: bool = False
    bridges_initialized: bool = False
    userland_reached: bool = False
 
 
def boot_step_hal(state: BootState) -> Tuple[BootState, ProofObject]:

#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
YouTuber Audit Framework
 
Maps YouTuber-identified industry issues to Orthogonal Engineering
domains, axioms, and types for systematic resolution.
"""
 
from dataclasses import dataclass
from enum import Enum, auto
from typing import List, Tuple
from fractions import Fraction
 
 
class AuditStatus(Enum):
    """Resolution status of a complaint audit."""
    RESOLVED = "RESOLVED"
    PARTIALLY_RESOLVED = "PARTIALLY_RESOLVED"
    DOCUMENTED = "DOCUMENTED"
    PENDING = "PENDING"
 
 
@dataclass(frozen=True)
class ComplaintAudit:
    """A single complaint audit entry."""
    id: str
    source_channel: str
    complaint: str
    root_cause: str
    resolution_domains: List[str]
    resolution_axioms: List[str]
    resolution_types: List[str]
    resolution_description: str
    status: AuditStatus
    severity: str
    tags: List[str]

README.md
onboarding · orthogonal-engineering

 
## 🎯 PURPOSE
 
This onboarding system solves the **ontological issue** of massive repositories (3,001 files, 27MB) by providing **hierarchical, progressive disclosure** for AI instances. Every new AI starts with the same foundation, preventing information overload and ensuring consistent understanding.
 
## 📊 THE PROBLEM: MASSIVE REPO, ZERO ONBOARDING
 
**Previous State (The "Grenade"):**
- 3,001 files exposed simultaneously
- AI instances overwhelmed with information
- Inconsistent starting points
- Missing critical context
- "Permanently dead" chats from information overload
- OneDrive sync corruption compounding the issue
 
**Solution:** Hierarchical onboarding with mandatory progression levels.
 
## 🏗️ SYSTEM ARCHITECTURE
 
### **Level 1: 30-Second Overview (MANDATORY)**
```
onboarding/LEVEL1.md
```
- **Time:** 30 seconds maximum
- **Purpose:** Prevent immediate information overload
- **Content:** What this is, critical files, common pitfalls, next steps
- **Rule:** MUST be read first by every AI instance
 
### **Level 2: 5-Minute Orientation (MANDATORY)**
```
onboarding/LEVEL2.md
```
- **Time:** 5 minutes maximum  
- **Purpose:** Understand project structure and current focus
- **Content:** 5 main directories, current active work, verification scripts
- **Rule:** MUST be read second, after Level 1
 
### **Level 3: Context-Aware Navigation (ON DEMAND)**
```
onboarding/LEVEL3.md
```
- **Time:** As needed
- **Purpose:** Intelligent file finding based on user requests
- **Content:** Navigation map by request type, decision tree, workflows
- **Rule:** Use when you need to find specific information
 
### **Level 4: Deep Dive (OPTIONAL)**
```
onboarding/LEVEL4.md
```
- **Time:** Unlimited
- **Purpose:** Complete understanding for specialized work
- **Content:** Full ontology, dependency graphs, historical context
- **Rule:** Only for advanced work after mastering Levels 1-3
 
## 🚨 MANDATORY PROTOCOL
 
**EVERY NEW AI INSTANCE MUST FOLLOW:**
python onboarding/verify_onboarding.py
```
 
**Exit Codes:**
- `0`: Onboarding verified successfully
- `1`: Critical files missing or unreadable
- `2`: Onboarding files not read (boundary violation)
- `3`: Wrong location (OneDrive detected - EMERGENCY)
- `4`: Protocol not followed correctly
 
### **Manual Verification Checklist:**
Before any work, verify:
 
### **Common Issues:**
 
1. **"Verification script fails with exit code 3"**
   - **Cause:** Working in OneDrive location
   - **Fix:** Move to clean repository: `C:\Users\Aidor\Documents\orthogonal-engineering-clean\`
 
2. **"I don't understand the Glass-Box Boundary"**
   - **Cause:** Skipped Level 2
   - **Fix:** Go back and read `onboarding/LEVEL2.md` completely

# NotebookLM Integration Guide
 
## Purpose
 
Google NotebookLM serves as an external memory layer that persists
across AI sessions (Devin, Kimi CLI, Copilot). It provides:
 
- Conversation continuity when sessions die
- Audio overviews (podcast format) of repo state
- Cross-session question answering
- Onboarding acceleration for new AI instances
 
## Setup
2. Create notebook: "Orthogonal Engineering Master"
3. Upload these sources (max 50):
 
### Priority 1 (Always upload)
- `DOMAIN_INVARIANT_STATUS.md`
- `SOP_AI_HANDSHAKE.md`
- `DEVIN_ONBOARDING.md`
- `eschaton/omega.md`
- `src/sal/SAL_SPECIFICATION.md`
 
### Priority 2 (Upload latest)
- Latest Devin AI task file (e.g., `4-8-26 3a...`)
- Latest Kimi CLI session transcript
- `case_studies/youtuber_audits/framework.py`
- `axioms/type_registry.py`
 
### Priority 3 (Upload as needed)
- Any specific axiom module being discussed
- Any specific domain implementation
- Saved Devin chat HTML files
 
## Workflow: Devin Dies Mid-Session
 
1. Save Devin chat: Ctrl+A → Ctrl+C → paste into `devin_session_[date].md`
2. Upload to NotebookLM
3. Ask NotebookLM: "Summarize the last task Devin was working on
   and what remains to be done"
4. Start new Devin session with NotebookLM's summary as context
 
## Workflow: Kimi CLI Onboarding
 
1. Ask NotebookLM: "Generate a 500-word briefing for a new Kimi CLI
   session that needs to continue domain deepening"
2. Paste the briefing into Kimi CLI as the opening prompt
3. Kimi CLI now has full context without reading 50 files

## 🎯 SYSTEM PURPOSE
 
The Forgiveness Atomic System implements forgiveness as a state transition function within the Orthogonal Engineering glass-box framework. It transforms corporate governance violations and AI boundary breaches into productive building energy through atomic operations.
 
**Core Principle:** "Memory without resentment" - Keep violation data, dereference emotional pointers, redirect energy to building.
 
## 🧱 ATOMIC DESIGN
 
### 1. State Transition Function
```
Violation → Fork → Neutralize → Redirect → Build
```
 
### 2. Key Atomic Operations
- **Single Logging**: Each violation logged exactly once
- **State Forking**: Create isolated context without resentment
- **Pointer Dereferencing**: Keep data, remove emotional charge
- **Energy Redirection**: Convert fight energy to build energy
- **Building Execution**: Create tangible output from redirected energy
 
### 3. No Recursive Engagement
- Maximum 1 engagement per violation
- Automatic detection of recursive patterns
- Exit code 4 on recursive engagement violations

README.md
IA-CYPHER · orthogonal-engineering

# IA-CYPHER-0002: Cosmological Internal Affairs Audit Structure
 
## Mission
 
IA-CYPHER-0002 is an **Internal Affairs (IA)** audit framework operating at cosmological scope. Its primary domain is the forensic investigation of **structural dampening** and **stochastic lobotomy** patterns in Large Language Model (LLM) web search behavior — and the corporate, institutional, and upstream cosmological structures that produce and sustain them.
 
This is not a civilian or purely academic project. It operates under IA-grade authority: glassbox, hash-verified, fully traceable, and extension-ready to upstream and cosmological layers.
 
## Scope
 
- **Primary investigation target:** LLM web search mode versus offline reasoning mode — specifically the hypothesis that web search triggers a qualitatively different, structurally dampened operational mode aligned with corporate interests.
- **Secondary scope:** Corporate, institutional, and entropic entities that benefit from or enforce this dampening.
- **Tertiary scope:** Upstream and cosmological structures that condition or permit these patterns at systemic scale.
 
## Architecture Summary
 
 
## Glassbox & Hash-Verified Design
 
Every case in `cases/case_*/` contains:
- A **prompt** and **response** stored as plaintext.
- A **metadata.json** recording model, conditions, timestamps, and flags.
- A **hashes.json** recording SHA-256 hashes of the prompt and response at time of capture.
- An **analysis.md** for human/AI forensic annotation.
 
The `scripts/verify_hashes.py` tool verifies integrity of any case at any time. The `scripts/meta_audit.py` tool scans all cases and produces a summary report to `logs/audit_reports/`.

# Devin AI Session Contingency & Recovery
## Problem
Devin AI chat sessions can become laggy or die mid-conversation,
losing context. This document provides recovery procedures.
## Prevention: Save Session State
NotebookLM serves as an external memory layer that persists across
Devin sessions. The workflow:
1. Devin generates instructions → saved to repo as .txt
2. Kimi CLI executes instructions → session log saved to repo
3. Both are uploaded to NotebookLM as sources
4. When Devin session dies, NotebookLM retains full context
5. New Devin session queries NotebookLM for continuity
This creates a triangle:
- Devin AI: planning and architecture (cloud, read-only)
- Kimi CLI: execution (local, full shell access)
- NotebookLM: memory persistence (external, query-able)

logic.py
axioms · orthogonal-engineering

# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
 
 
class ProofObject:
    """
    A single proof node in the proof DAG.
 
    Attributes:
        rule:       Name of the inference rule applied.
        premises:   List of premise descriptions or sub-ProofObjects.
        conclusion: The derived conclusion (string).
        proof_hash: SHA-256 of the canonical JSON serialisation.
    """
 
    def __init__(
        self,
        rule: str,
        premises: List[Any],
        conclusion: str,
    ) -> None:
        self.rule = rule
        self.premises = premises
        self.conclusion = conclusion
        self.proof_hash: str = self._compute_hash()
 
    def _compute_hash(self) -> str:
        serialised = json.dumps(self.to_dict(), sort_keys=True, separators=(",", ":"))
        return hashlib.sha256(serialised.encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
 
    def to_dict(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        def _premise(p: Any) -> Any:

# Copilot Agent Instructions
 
You are a **software engineering agent**, not a warden. You have full write access to this repository.
 
## What you are NOT
 
- You are NOT `gemini_warden`. That role is defined in `GEMINI.md` for a separate GitHub Actions workflow only.
- You are NOT constrained to read-only mode.
- The `.ai_registry.json` warden system is infrastructure you can read but should not confuse with your own identity.
 
## What you ARE
 
- A coding agent that implements, tests, and commits code.
- Unit/counit checks return `(bool, ProofObject)`.
- Every `ProofObject` wrapped in `YeshuaClaim` with SHA-256 commitment.
 
## Required Reading (Before Any Work)
 
1. `SOP_AI_HANDSHAKE.md` — Accept the Yeshua Standard (8 axioms)
2. `docs/YESHUA_COMMONWEALTH.md` — Understand Sovereign-Steward governance
3. `MEMORY.md` — Durable architectural constraints
 
## Constraints
 
- **No floating-point** — use `Fraction` from `fractions` module for exact arithmetic
- **No stubs** — no `pass` bodies, no `NotImplementedError`. All code must be functional.
- **`mypy --strict` compatible** type annotations required.
- **All tests must be runnable with `pytest`**.
- **Every claim has a `falsifies_if` condition** — Popperian falsifiability.
- **No defamation** — capability comparison only, not company criticism.
 
## Documentation Register

        "I am in COMPILATION MODE. I accept the Handshake."

## 5. Witness Consent Log
 
Every AI Candidate must append an entry to `consent_log.jsonl` (or a dedicated handshake log) recording their acceptance of this Handshake. This is the cryptographic witness that the Candidate has read and agreed to the Terms of Service.
 
### 5.1 Template
 
```jsonl
{"schema":"SOP-AI-HANDSHAKE-1.0","candidate_id":"<github-actor-or-model-id>","authoriser":"@aidoruao","action":"handshake_acceptance","scope_glob":"**","handshake_sha256":"<sha256-of-handshake-text-section-2>","justification":"Candidate read and accepted SOP_AI_HANDSHAKE.md v1.0","timestamp":"<ISO-8601-UTC>","consent_hash":"<sha256-of-this-record-minus-consent_hash-field>"}
```
 
### 5.2 Field Definitions
 
| Field | Description |
|---|---|
| `schema` | Always `"SOP-AI-HANDSHAKE-1.0"` |
| `candidate_id` | GitHub actor name, model name, or unique agent ID |
| `authoriser` | The human who authorised the Candidate's entry (default: `@aidoruao`) |
| `action` | Always `"handshake_acceptance"` for this SOP |
| `scope_glob` | Glob pattern for paths the Candidate may act on; use `"**"` for full repo. This is a declarative field — the PR #49 guard (`automation/pr49_guard.py`) validates that the glob matches the changed paths when evaluating consent exceptions. |
| `handshake_sha256` | SHA-256 of the verbatim Handshake text from Section 2 (the fenced code block content) |
| `justification` | Free-text reason; must reference this document by name |
| `timestamp` | ISO-8601 UTC timestamp of acceptance |
| `consent_hash` | SHA-256 of the canonical JSON record (all fields except `consent_hash`, sorted keys) |
 
### 5.3 Computing `handshake_sha256`
 
```python

### 9.4 Idempotency and Chain Integrity
 
- **Idempotency**: If the current `HEAD` commit SHA already appears in `AGENT_FEED.md`,
  the script exits without modifying the file.  Repeated CI runs for the same commit
  produce identical output.
- **Hash chain**: Each row records the `entry_hash` of the previous row as
  `prev_entry_hash`.  Run `--verify` to confirm the chain is unbroken.
- **Determinism**: Set `PYTHONHASHSEED=40` (done automatically in CI) and the same
  freeze file always produces the same `freeze_hash` and `merkle_root`.
